This directory contains code for the\n    78→[_istioctl_](https://istio.io/latest/docs/reference/commands/istioctl/) command line utility.\n    79→\n    80→    - [pilot](pilot/). This directory contains [security](https://istio.io/latest/docs/concepts/security/) related code.\n    87→\n    88→- [istio/proxy](https://github.com/istio/proxy). Each issue we track has a variety of metadata:\n   104→\n   105→- **Epic**. An epic represents a feature area for Istio as a whole. Epics are fairly broad in scope and are basically product-level things.\n   106→Each issue is ultimately part of an epic.\n   107→\n   108→- **Milestone**. Each issue is assigned a milestone. This is 0.1, 0.2, ..., or 'Nebulous Future'. The milestone indicates when we\n   109→think the issue should get addressed.\n   110→\n   111→- **Priority**. Each issue has a priority which is represented by the column in the [Prioritization](https://github.com/orgs/istio/projects/6) project. Priority can be one of\n   112→P0, P1, P2, or >P2. The priority indicates how important it is to address the issue within the milestone. P0 says that the\n   113→milestone cannot be considered achieved if the issue isn't resolved.\n   114→\n   115→---\n   116→\n   117→<div align=\"center\">\n   118→    <picture>\n   119→      <source media=\"(prefers-color-scheme: dark)\" srcset=\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/cncf/artwork/refs/heads/main/other/cncf/horizontal/color-whitetext/cncf-color-whitetext.svg\">\n   120→      <source media=\"(prefers-color-scheme: light)\" srcset=\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/cncf/artwork/master/other/cncf/horizontal/color/cncf-color.svg\">\n   121→      <img width=\"300\" alt=\"Cloud Native Computing Foundation logo\" src=\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/cncf/artwork/refs/heads/main/other/cncf/horizontal/color-whitetext/cncf-color-whitetext.svg\">\n   122→    </picture>\n   123→    <p>Istio is a <a href=\"https://cncf.io\">Cloud Native Computing Foundation</a> project.</p>\n   124→</div>\n   125→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Istio’s powerful features provide a uniform and more efficient way to secure, connect, and monitor services. Istio is the path to load balancing, service-to-service authentication, and monitoring – with few or no service code changes.\n\n- For in-depth information about how to use Istio, visit [istio.io](https://istio.io)\n- To ask questions and get assistance from our community, visit [GitHub Discussions](https://github.com/istio/istio/discussions)\n- To learn how to participate in our overall community, visit [our community page](https://istio.io/about/community)\n\nIn this README:\n\n- [Introduction](#introduction)\n- [Repositories](#repositories)\n- [Issue management](#issue-management)\n\nIn addition, here are some other documents you may wish to read:\n\n- [Istio Community](https://github.com/istio/community#istio-community) - describes how to get involved and contribute to the Istio project\n- [Istio Developer's Guide](https://github.com/istio/istio/wiki/Preparing-for-Development) - explains how to set up and use an Istio development environment\n- [Project Conventions](https://github.com/istio/istio/wiki/Development-Conventions) - describes the conventions we use within the code base\n- [Creating Fast and Lean Code](https://github.com/istio/istio/wiki/Writing-Fast-and-Lean-Code) - performance-oriented advice and guidelines for the code base\n\nYou'll find many other useful documents on our [Wiki](https://github.com/istio/istio/wiki).\n\n## Introduction\n\n[Istio](https://istio.io/latest/docs/concepts/what-is-istio/) is an open platform for providing a uniform way to [integrate\nmicroservices](https://istio.io/latest/docs/examples/microservices-istio/), manage [traffic flow](https://istio.io/latest/docs/concepts/traffic-management/) across microservices, enforce policies\nand aggregate telemetry data. Istio's control plane provides an abstraction\nlayer over the underlying cluster management platform, such as Kubernetes.\n\nIstio is composed of these components:\n\n- **Envoy** - Sidecar proxies per microservice to handle ingress/egress traffic\n   between services in the cluster and from a service to external\n   services. The proxies form a _secure microservice mesh_ providing a rich\n   set of functions like discovery, rich layer-7 routing, circuit breakers,\n   policy enforcement and telemetry recording/reporting\n   functions.\n\n  > Note: The service mesh is not an overlay network. It\n  > simplifies and enhances how microservices in an application talk to each\n  > other over the network provided by the underlying platform.\n\n* **Ztunnel** - A lightweight data plane proxy written in Rust,\n    used in Ambient mesh mode to provide secure connectivity and observability for workloads without sidecar proxies.\n\n- **Istiod** - The Istio control plane. It provides service discovery, configuration and certificate management.\n\n## Repositories\n\nThe Istio project is divided across a few GitHub repositories:\n\n- [istio/api](https://github.com/istio/api). This repository defines\ncomponent-level APIs and common configuration formats for the Istio platform.\n\n- [istio/community](https://github.com/istio/community). This repository contains\ninformation on the Istio community, including the various documents that govern\nthe Istio open source project.\n\n- [istio/istio](README.md). This is the main code repository. It hosts Istio's\ncore components, install artifacts, and sample programs. It includes:\n\n    - [istioctl](istioctl/). This directory contains code for the\n[_istioctl_](https://istio.io/latest/docs/reference/commands/istioctl/) command line utility.\n\n    - [pilot](pilot/). This directory\ncontains platform-specific code to populate the\n[abstract service model](https://istio.io/docs/concepts/traffic-management/#pilot), dynamically reconfigure the proxies\nwhen the application topology changes, as well as translate\n[routing rules](https://istio.io/latest/docs/reference/config/networking/) into proxy specific configuration.\n\n    - [security](security/). This directory contains [security](https://istio.io/latest/docs/concepts/security/) related code.\n\n- [istio/proxy](https://github.com/istio/proxy). The Istio proxy contains\nextensions to the [Envoy proxy](https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy) (in the form of\nEnvoy filters) that support authentication, authorization, and telemetry collection.\n\n- [istio/ztunnel](https://github.com/istio/ztunnel). The repository contains the Rust implementation of the ztunnel\ncomponent of Ambient mesh.\n\n- [istio/client-go](https://github.com/istio/client-go). This repository defines\n  auto-generated Kubernetes clients for interacting with Istio resources programmatically.\n\n> [!NOTE]\n> Only the `istio/api` and `istio/client-go` repositories expose stable interfaces intended for direct usage as libraries.\n\n## Issue management\n\nWe use GitHub to track all of our bugs and feature requests. Each issue we track has a variety of metadata:\n\n- **Epic**. An epic represents a feature area for Istio as a whole. Epics are fairly broad in scope and are basically product-level things.\nEach issue is ultimately part of an epic.\n\n- **Milestone**. Each issue is assigned a milestone. This is 0.1, 0.2, ..., or 'Nebulous Future'. The milestone indicates when we\nthink the issue should get addressed.\n\n- **Priority**. Each issue has a priority which is represented by the column in the [Prioritization](https://github.com/orgs/istio/projects/6) project. Priority can be one of\nP0, P1, P2, or >P2. The priority indicates how important it is to address the issue within the milestone. P0 says that the\nmilestone cannot be considered achieved if the issue isn't resolved.\n\n---\n\n<div align=\"center\">\n    <picture>\n      <source media=\"(prefers-color-scheme: dark)\" srcset=\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/cncf/artwork/refs/heads/main/other/cncf/horizontal/color-whitetext/cncf-color-whitetext.svg\">\n      <source media=\"(prefers-color-scheme: light)\" srcset=\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/cncf/artwork/master/other/cncf/horizontal/color/cncf-color.svg\">\n      <img width=\"300\" alt=\"Cloud Native Computing Foundation logo\" src=\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/cncf/artwork/refs/heads/main/other/cncf/horizontal/color-whitetext/cncf-color-whitetext.svg\">\n    </picture>\n    <p>Istio is a <a href=\"https://cncf.io\">Cloud Native Computing Foundation</a> project.</p>\n</div>\n","numLines":125,"startLine":1,"totalLines":125}}}

This is not used buts adds many MB to Envoy protos\n# vtprotobuf: enables optimized protobuf marshalling.\nSTANDARD_TAGS=vtprotobuf,disable_pgv\n\n.PHONY: build\nbuild: depend ## Builds all go binaries.\n\tGOOS=$(GOOS_LOCAL) GOARCH=$(GOARCH_LOCAL) LDFLAGS=$(RELEASE_LDFLAGS) common/scripts/gobuild.sh $(TARGET_OUT)/ -tags=$(STANDARD_TAGS) $(STANDARD_BINARIES)\n\tGOOS=$(GOOS_LOCAL) GOARCH=$(GOARCH_LOCAL) LDFLAGS=$(RELEASE_LDFLAGS) common/scripts/gobuild.sh $(TARGET_OUT)/ -tags=$(AGENT_TAGS) $(AGENT_BINARIES)\n\n# The build-linux target is responsible for building binaries used within containers.\n# This target should be expanded upon as we add more Linux architectures: i.e. build-arm64.\n# Then a new build target can be created such as build-container-bin that builds these\n# various platform images.\n.PHONY: build-linux\nbuild-linux: depend\n\tGOOS=linux GOARCH=$(GOARCH_LOCAL) LDFLAGS=$(RELEASE_LDFLAGS) common/scripts/gobuild.sh $(TARGET_OUT_LINUX)/ -tags=$(STANDARD_TAGS) $(STANDARD_BINARIES)\n\tGOOS=linux GOARCH=$(GOARCH_LOCAL) LDFLAGS=$(RELEASE_LDFLAGS) common/scripts/gobuild.sh $(TARGET_OUT_LINUX)/ -tags=$(AGENT_TAGS) $(LINUX_AGENT_BINARIES)\n\n.PHONY: build-cni\nbuild-cni: depend\n\tGOOS=$(GOOS_LOCAL) GOARCH=$(GOARCH_LOCAL) LDFLAGS=$(RELEASE_LDFLAGS) common/scripts/gobuild.sh $(TARGET_OUT)/ -tags=$(AGENT_TAGS) $(CNI_BINARIES)\n\n# Create targets for TARGET_OUT_LINUX/binary\n# There are two use cases here:\n# * Building all docker images (generally in CI). In this case we want to build everything at once, so they share work\n# * Building a single docker image (generally during dev). In this case we just want to build the single binary alone\nBUILD_ALL ?= true\ndefine build-linux\n.PHONY: $(TARGET_OUT_LINUX)/$(shell basename $(1))\nifeq ($(BUILD_ALL),true)\n$(TARGET_OUT_LINUX)/$(shell basename $(1)): build-linux\n\t@:\nelse\n$(TARGET_OUT_LINUX)/$(shell basename $(1)): $(TARGET_OUT_LINUX)\n\tGOOS=linux GOARCH=$(GOARCH_LOCAL) LDFLAGS=$(RELEASE_LDFLAGS) common/scripts/gobuild.sh $(TARGET_OUT_LINUX)/ -tags=$(2) $(1)\nendif\nendef\n\n$(foreach bin,$(STANDARD_BINARIES),$(eval $(call build-linux,$(bin),$(STANDARD_TAGS))))\n$(foreach bin,$(LINUX_AGENT_BINARIES),$(eval $(call build-linux,$(bin),$(AGENT_TAGS))))\n\n# Create helper targets for each binary, like \"pilot-discovery\"\n# As an optimization, these still build everything\n$(foreach bin,$(BINARIES),$(shell basename $(bin))): build\nifneq ($(TARGET_OUT_LINUX),$(LOCAL_OUT))\n# if we are on linux already, then this rule is handled by build-linux above, which handles BUILD_ALL variable\n$(foreach bin,$(BINARIES),${LOCAL_OUT}/$(shell basename $(bin))): build","numLines":80,"startLine":200,"totalLines":504}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01G4XgBNeiCVFSg9e5L7YnZN","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01EShM3kUniS7iMKJmw2orYF","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Istio Control Plane Developer Onboarding Guide\n\nWelcome to the Istio project! This guide will help you get started with development on Istio's control plane. By the end, you'll be able to build the core components, understand the architecture, and submit your first contribution.\n\n---\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Build Prerequisites](#build-prerequisites)\n2. [Architecture Overview](#architecture-overview)\n3. [First Contribution Workflow](#first-contribution-workflow)\n\n---\n\n## Build Prerequisites\n\n### Required Go Version\n\nIstio's control plane requires **Go 1.25.0 or later**. Check your version:\n\n```bash\ngo version\n```\n\nIf you need to install or update Go, visit [golang.org](https://golang.org).\n\n### Environment Setup\n\nThe Istio build system uses environment variables to control the build process. Key variables include:\n\n- `GOPATH` - Your Go workspace path (automatically detected)\n- `GOPROXY` - Go module proxy (defaults to `https://proxy.golang.org`)\n- `GO111MODULE` - Enables Go modules (defaults to `on`)\n- `BUILD_WITH_CONTAINER` - Set to `1` to use Docker for builds (optional; defaults to local build)\n\n### Cloning the Repository\n\nClone the repository with all submodules:\n\n```bash\ngit clone https://github.com/istio/istio.git\ncd istio\n```\n\nThe repository structure includes:\n- `pilot/` - Service discovery and traffic management (Pilot)\n- `security/` - Certificate management and security policies (Citadel)\n- `pkg/` - Shared packages (XDS, bootstrap, configuration)\n- `istioctl/` - Command-line tool\n- `tests/` - Integration and unit tests\n\n### Building the Control Plane Binaries\n\nThe main control plane binary is **istiod** (Istio daemon), which combines Pilot, Citadel, and Galley into a single process.\n\nBefore building, initialize dependencies:\n\n```bash\nmake init\n```\n\nThis downloads Envoy binaries and other required dependencies defined in `istio.deps`.\n\n#### Building the pilot-discovery Binary\n\nPilot-discovery is the core control plane service that provides service discovery and configuration to Envoy proxies via the xDS protocol:\n\n```bash\nmake pilot-discovery\n```\n\nOr directly with Make:\n\n```bash\nmake build\n```\n\nThis builds all binaries, including:\n- `pilot-discovery` - The discovery service (located at `pilot/cmd/pilot-discovery`)\n- `pilot-agent` - The sidecar proxy agent (located at `pilot/cmd/pilot-agent`)\n- `istioctl` - The command-line interface\n- Other utilities\n\nThe compiled binaries are placed in the `$GOBIN` directory (typically `$GOPATH/bin`).\n\n#### Building Individual Binaries\n\nTo build a specific binary:\n\n```bash\nmake <binary-name>\n```\n\nFor example:\n```bash\nmake istioctl\nmake pilot-agent\n```\n\n### Running Tests\n\nThe test suite uses race detection to catch concurrency issues:\n\n```bash\nmake test\n```\n\nOr specifically for the Pilot component:\n\n```bash\nPKG=./pilot/... make test\n```\n\nFor a specific package:\n\n```bash\ngo test -race ./pilot/pkg/model/...\n```\n\n### Lint and Code Quality\n\nBefore submitting a PR, run the linters and formatters:\n\n```bash\nmake precommit\n```\n\nThis runs:\n- `make fmt` - Auto-formats Go code using `gofmt`\n- `make lint` - Runs all linters (Go, Python, YAML, Helm, etc.)\n\nFor Go specifically:\n\n```bash\nmake format-go\n```\n\nThis uses `gofmt` to format all Go files consistently.\n\n### Setting Up Your Environment (Local Build)\n\nIf building locally (not in a container), the Makefile automatically sets up the environment:\n\n```bash\n# The setup happens automatically during make\n# But you can manually verify your environment:\nmake show.goenv  # Shows Go environment\nmake show.env    # Shows all environment variables\n```\n\n---\n\n## Architecture Overview\n\n### Control Plane Components\n\nIstio's control plane (istiod) is composed of three major subsystems that have been merged into a single binary:\n\n#### 1. **Pilot** (`pilot/pkg/`)\n\nPilot is responsible for service discovery and dynamic configuration.\n\n**Key responsibilities:**\n- Discovers services from Kubernetes, Consul, or other service registries\n- Translates high-level Istio routing rules (VirtualService, DestinationRule) into Envoy-specific configuration\n- Implements the xDS protocol to push configuration to Envoy proxies\n- Manages load balancing, retries, and traffic policies\n\n**Key packages:**\n- `pilot/pkg/model/` - Core data models (ServiceInstance, Gateway, EnvoyFilter)\n- `pilot/pkg/networking/` - Configuration generation for Envoy\n- `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/` - Abstraction layer for different service discovery backends\n- `pilot/pkg/xds/` - xDS protocol implementation\n\n#### 2. **Citadel** (`security/pkg/`)\n\nCitadel is the security component responsible for certificate and key management.\n\n**Key responsibilities:**\n- Issues and rotates mTLS certificates for workloads\n- Manages the Istio CA (Certificate Authority)\n- Enforces authentication policies (PeerAuthentication)\n- Handles certificate distribution to Envoy proxies\n\n**Key packages:**\n- `security/pkg/pki/` - Public key infrastructure and certificate generation\n- `security/pkg/k8s/` - Kubernetes-specific security operations\n- `security/pkg/nodeagent/` - Agent running on each node for local certificate management\n\n#### 3. **Galley** (Now merged into Pilot)\n\nGalley's role of configuration validation and distribution has been integrated into Pilot. Configuration analysis still exists in:\n\n- `pkg/config/analysis/` - Configuration validation and diagnostics\n\n### The xDS Protocol\n\nThe **xDS protocol** (Envoy's discovery services) is how Istio's control plane communicates with Envoy proxies. It's a gRPC-based protocol for dynamic configuration delivery.\n\n**xDS Types:**\n- **Cluster Discovery Service (CDS)** - Tells proxies about backend services\n- **Endpoint Discovery Service (EDS)** - Lists healthy endpoints for a service\n- **Listener Discovery Service (LDS)** - Defines how to listen for incoming traffic\n- **Route Discovery Service (RDS)** - Defines routing rules\n- **Secret Discovery Service (SDS)** - Delivers TLS certificates\n\n### Data Flow: Service Discovery to xDS Push\n\nHere's an end-to-end example of how a service discovery update triggers an xDS push:\n\n1. **Service Registry Update**\n   - A Kubernetes pod is created in the cluster\n   - Pilot's Kubernetes controller watches the API server\n   - The controller detects the new pod and updates the `ServiceInstance` model\n\n2. **Model Update**\n   - Pilot's `Environment` (in `pilot/pkg/model/context.go`) maintains all discovered services\n   - When a `ServiceInstance` changes, the controller notifies the environment via `XDSUpdater`\n\n3. **Configuration Generation**\n   - The networking layer (`pilot/pkg/networking/`) generates Envoy configuration\n   - For the new endpoint, it creates or updates:\n     - An Envoy `Cluster` (the backend service definition)\n     - `Endpoints` (the specific pod IP and port)\n\n4. **xDS Push**\n   - Pilot's xDS server (in `pilot/pkg/xds/`) maintains connections to all Envoy proxies\n   - When configuration changes, it sends:\n     - **EDS update** with the new endpoint\n     - **CDS update** if the cluster definition changed\n     - **RDS update** if routing rules changed\n   - Each update is accompanied by a version number for consistency checking\n\n5. **Envoy Updates**\n   - Envoy proxies receive the xDS update\n   - They validate and apply the new configuration\n   - Traffic to the new endpoint begins flowing\n\n**Key files for this flow:**\n- `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller.go` - Kubernetes controller watching services/endpoints\n- `pilot/pkg/model/context.go` - The `Environment` and `PushContext` that maintain state\n- `pilot/pkg/networking/core/v1alpha3/` - Config builders for Envoy resources\n- `pilot/pkg/xds/v3/ads.go` - Aggregated Discovery Service (ADS) implementation\n\n### Service Registry Integration\n\nPilot uses an abstraction layer to support multiple service discovery backends:\n\n**Service Registry Interface** (`pilot/pkg/model/service.go`):\n- `ServiceInstance` - A single service instance (pod, VM, etc.)\n- `Service` - A logical service with multiple instances\n- `ServiceRegistry` - Interface for discovering services\n\n**Supported Backends** (`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/`):\n- `kube/` - Kubernetes native service discovery\n- `serviceentry/` - ServiceEntry custom resource\n- `memory/` - In-memory registry (testing)\n- `aggregate/` - Aggregates multiple registries\n\nWhen Pilot starts, it initializes service registries and watches them for changes. The aggregate registry combines multiple sources, allowing a single control plane to work across hybrid environments.\n\n### Key Packages\n\n| Package | Purpose |\n|---------|---------|\n| `pilot/pkg/model/` | Core data models and context |\n| `pilot/pkg/networking/` | Config generation for Envoy |\n| `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/` | Service discovery abstraction |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/` | xDS protocol implementation |\n| `pilot/pkg/bootstrap/` | Pilot startup and initialization |\n| `security/pkg/pki/` | Certificate generation and management |\n| `pkg/config/` | Istio configuration types and validation |\n| `pkg/kube/` | Kubernetes client utilities |\n\n---\n\n## First Contribution Workflow\n\n### Finding Good First Issues\n\nThe Istio project uses GitHub issues to track work. To find issues suitable for new contributors:\n\n1. Visit [github.com/istio/istio/issues](https://github.com/istio/istio/issues)\n2. Filter by labels:\n   - `good-first-issue` - Ideal for beginners\n   - `help-wanted` - Community help is welcome\n   - `kind/bug` - Bug fixes are always valuable\n3. Check the issue for:\n   - A clear problem statement\n   - Reproduction steps (for bugs)\n   - Expected vs. actual behavior\n\n### Development Workflow\n\n#### 1. Fork and Branch\n\nFork the repository on GitHub and create a feature branch:\n\n```bash\ngit checkout -b fix/issue-name\n```\n\n#### 2. Make Your Changes\n\nEdit the code in your branch. For example, if fixing an issue in Pilot:\n\n```bash\n# Edit the relevant file\nvim pilot/pkg/model/service.go\n\n# Or if it's a test file\nvim pilot/pkg/model/service_test.go\n```\n\n#### 3. Run Pre-commit Checks\n\nBefore committing, run the linters and formatters:\n\n```bash\nmake precommit\n```\n\nThis ensures your code matches Istio's style guide. If there are formatting issues, the formatters will fix them automatically.\n\n#### 4. Run Tests\n\nAlways run tests for the package you modified:\n\n```bash\n# Run tests for a specific package\nPKG=./pilot/pkg/model make test\n\n# Or run tests for a broader area\ngo test -race ./pilot/...\n```\n\nIf you're adding a new feature, add unit tests:\n\n```go\n// In pilot/pkg/model/service_test.go\nfunc TestMyNewFeature(t *testing.T) {\n    // Setup\n    svc := &Service{...}\n\n    // Action\n    result := svc.MyNewMethod()\n\n    // Assert\n    if result != expected {\n        t.Errorf(\"got %v, want %v\", result, expected)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### 5. Build and Verify\n\nBuild the affected components:\n\n```bash\nmake build\n```\n\nOr just the binary you're interested in:\n\n```bash\nmake pilot-discovery\n```\n\nIf you're modifying security code:\n\n```bash\nPKG=./security/... make test\n```\n\n### Writing Unit Tests\n\nIstio uses the Go testing package. Here's the pattern:\n\n```go\npackage model\n\nimport \"testing\"\n\nfunc TestMyFunction(t *testing.T) {\n    // Arrange: Set up test data\n    input := \"test\"\n\n    // Act: Call the function\n    result := MyFunction(input)\n\n    // Assert: Check the result\n    expected := \"expected output\"\n    if result != expected {\n        t.Errorf(\"MyFunction(%q) = %q, want %q\", input, result, expected)\n    }\n}\n```\n\nRun tests with race detection (recommended):\n\n```bash\ngo test -race ./pilot/pkg/model/...\n```\n\n### Submitting a Pull Request\n\n#### Create the PR\n\nPush your branch and open a pull request on GitHub:\n\n```bash\ngit push origin fix/issue-name\n```\n\nThen visit [github.com/istio/istio/pulls](https://github.com/istio/istio/pulls) and create a new PR from your branch.\n\n#### PR Description\n\nWrite a clear PR description that includes:\n\n```markdown\n## Description\nWhat does this PR do? Link any related issues.\n\nFixes #123\n\n## Changes\n- Detailed list of changes\n- One bullet per logical change\n\n## Testing\nHow was this tested?\n- Added unit tests for X\n- Manually tested Y\n\n## Checklist\n- [x] Code compiles\n- [x] Tests pass locally\n- [x] Linters pass\n- [x] No new TODOs\n```\n\n#### Required Reviewers\n\nThe `CODEOWNERS` file specifies required reviewers for each component:\n\n```\n/pilot/                                          @istio/wg-networking-maintainers\n/security/                                       @istio/wg-security-maintainers\n/pkg/config/                                     @istio/wg-networking-maintainers\n```\n\nEnsure your PR is assigned to the appropriate working group (WG). Use the PR template to auto-assign if available.\n\n#### CI Gates\n\nYour PR will automatically run:\n- **Unit tests** - All tests must pass\n- **Linters** - Code must pass style checks\n- **Build verification** - Binaries must compile on all supported platforms\n\nAll checks must pass before merging. If a check fails, the CI system will provide feedback in the PR comments.\n\n### Common Issues and Troubleshooting\n\n#### Build Fails: \"go: updates to go.mod needed\"\n\nThis happens when dependencies change. Fix it by running:\n\n```bash\ngo mod tidy\n```\n\nThen re-run the build:\n\n```bash\nmake build\n```\n\n#### Tests Fail with Import Errors\n\nMake sure you've run `make init` to download dependencies:\n\n```bash\nmake init\nmake test\n```\n\n#### \"Command not found\" when running Make\n\nThe Makefile expects to run in a container or with a properly configured environment. If you see this:\n\n```bash\n# Make sure you're in the root directory\ncd /path/to/istio\n\n# Run through Make, not directly\nmake pilot-discovery\n```\n\n#### Can't Find a Type or Function\n\nUse `grep` to search the codebase:\n\n```bash\n# Search for a type definition\ngrep -r \"type ServiceInstance struct\" pilot/\n\n# Search for function usage\ngrep -r \"MakeCluster(\" pilot/pkg/networking/\n```\n\nOr use your IDE's \"Go to Definition\" feature (Ctrl+Click in most editors).\n\n### Key References\n\n- **Contributing**: [github.com/istio/community/blob/master/CONTRIBUTING.md](https://github.com/istio/community/blob/master/CONTRIBUTING.md)\n- **Development Conventions**: [github.com/istio/istio/wiki/Development-Conventions](https://github.com/istio/istio/wiki/Development-Conventions)\n- **Code Style**: Istio follows Go's standard code style (enforced by `gofmt`)\n- **CODEOWNERS**: See `/CODEOWNERS` in the repo for who reviews what\n\n### Example: Making Your First Contribution\n\nLet's walk through fixing a simple bug in Pilot:\n\n**Step 1: Find an issue**\n- Browse `good-first-issue` labeled issues\n- Find: \"Service name validation could be more helpful\"\n\n**Step 2: Clone and branch**\n```bash\ngit clone https://github.com/YOUR_FORK/istio.git\ncd istio\ngit checkout -b improve/service-validation\n```\n\n**Step 3: Locate the code**\n```bash\n# Based on the issue, it's about services\ngrep -r \"Service validation\" pilot/pkg/\n# Found in pilot/pkg/model/service.go\n```\n\n**Step 4: Make changes**\n```bash\n# Edit the validation function\nvim pilot/pkg/model/service.go\n\n# Add a test\nvim pilot/pkg/model/service_test.go\n```\n\n**Step 5: Test locally**\n```bash\nmake precommit      # This guide will help you get started with development on Istio's control plane. By the end, you'll be able to build the core components, understand the architecture, and submit your first contribution.\n\n---\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Build Prerequisites](#build-prerequisites)\n2. [Architecture Overview](#architecture-overview)\n3. [First Contribution Workflow](#first-contribution-workflow)\n\n---\n\n## Build Prerequisites\n\n### Required Go Version\n\nIstio's control plane requires **Go 1.25.0 or later**. Check your version:\n\n```bash\ngo version\n```\n\nIf you need to install or update Go, visit [golang.org](https://golang.org).\n\n### Environment Setup\n\nThe Istio build system uses environment variables to control the build process. Key variables include:\n\n- `GOPATH` - Your Go workspace path (automatically detected)\n- `GOPROXY` - Go module proxy (defaults to `https://proxy.golang.org`)\n- `GO111MODULE` - Enables Go modules (defaults to `on`)\n- `BUILD_WITH_CONTAINER` - Set to `1` to use Docker for builds (optional; defaults to local build)\n\n### Cloning the Repository\n\nClone the repository with all submodules:\n\n```bash\ngit clone https://github.com/istio/istio.git\ncd istio\n```\n\nThe repository structure includes:\n- `pilot/` - Service discovery and traffic management (Pilot)\n- `security/` - Certificate management and security policies (Citadel)\n- `pkg/` - Shared packages (XDS, bootstrap, configuration)\n- `istioctl/` - Command-line tool\n- `tests/` - Integration and unit tests\n\n### Building the Control Plane Binaries\n\nThe main control plane binary is **istiod** (Istio daemon), which combines Pilot, Citadel, and Galley into a single process.\n\nBefore building, initialize dependencies:\n\n```bash\nmake init\n```\n\nThis downloads Envoy binaries and other required dependencies defined in `istio.deps`.\n\n#### Building the pilot-discovery Binary\n\nPilot-discovery is the core control plane service that provides service discovery and configuration to Envoy proxies via the xDS protocol:\n\n```bash\nmake pilot-discovery\n```\n\nOr directly with Make:\n\n```bash\nmake build\n```\n\nThis builds all binaries, including:\n- `pilot-discovery` - The discovery service (located at `pilot/cmd/pilot-discovery`)\n- `pilot-agent` - The sidecar proxy agent (located at `pilot/cmd/pilot-agent`)\n- `istioctl` - The command-line interface\n- Other utilities\n\nThe compiled binaries are placed in the `$GOBIN` directory (typically `$GOPATH/bin`).\n\n#### Building Individual Binaries\n\nTo build a specific binary:\n\n```bash\nmake <binary-name>\n```\n\nFor example:\n```bash\nmake istioctl\nmake pilot-agent\n```\n\n### Running Tests\n\nThe test suite uses race detection to catch concurrency issues:\n\n```bash\nmake test\n```\n\nOr specifically for the Pilot component:\n\n```bash\nPKG=./pilot/... make test\n```\n\nFor a specific package:\n\n```bash\ngo test -race ./pilot/pkg/model/...\n```\n\n### Lint and Code Quality\n\nBefore submitting a PR, run the linters and formatters:\n\n```bash\nmake precommit\n```\n\nThis runs:\n- `make fmt` - Auto-formats Go code using `gofmt`\n- `make lint` - Runs all linters (Go, Python, YAML, Helm, etc.)\n\nFor Go specifically:\n\n```bash\nmake format-go\n```\n\nThis uses `gofmt` to format all Go files consistently.\n\n### Setting Up Your Environment (Local Build)\n\nIf building locally (not in a container), the Makefile automatically sets up the environment:\n\n```bash\n# The setup happens automatically during make\n# But you can manually verify your environment:\nmake show.goenv  # Shows Go environment\nmake show.env    # Shows all environment variables\n```\n\n---\n\n## Architecture Overview\n\n### Control Plane Components\n\nIstio's control plane (istiod) is composed of three major subsystems that have been merged into a single binary:\n\n#### 1. **Pilot** (`pilot/pkg/`)\n\nPilot is responsible for service discovery and dynamic configuration.\n\n**Key responsibilities:**\n- Discovers services from Kubernetes, Consul, or other service registries\n- Translates high-level Istio routing rules (VirtualService, DestinationRule) into Envoy-specific configuration\n- Implements the xDS protocol to push configuration to Envoy proxies\n- Manages load balancing, retries, and traffic policies\n\n**Key packages:**\n- `pilot/pkg/model/` - Core data models (ServiceInstance, Gateway, EnvoyFilter)\n- `pilot/pkg/networking/` - Configuration generation for Envoy\n- `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/` - Abstraction layer for different service discovery backends\n- `pilot/pkg/xds/` - xDS protocol implementation\n\n#### 2. **Citadel** (`security/pkg/`)\n\nCitadel is the security component responsible for certificate and key management.\n\n**Key responsibilities:**\n- Issues and rotates mTLS certificates for workloads\n- Manages the Istio CA (Certificate Authority)\n- Enforces authentication policies (PeerAuthentication)\n- Handles certificate distribution to Envoy proxies\n\n**Key packages:**\n- `security/pkg/pki/` - Public key infrastructure and certificate generation\n- `security/pkg/k8s/` - Kubernetes-specific security operations\n- `security/pkg/nodeagent/` - Agent running on each node for local certificate management\n\n#### 3. **Galley** (Now merged into Pilot)\n\nGalley's role of configuration validation and distribution has been integrated into Pilot. Configuration analysis still exists in:\n\n- `pkg/config/analysis/` - Configuration validation and diagnostics\n\n### The xDS Protocol\n\nThe **xDS protocol** (Envoy's discovery services) is how Istio's control plane communicates with Envoy proxies. It's a gRPC-based protocol for dynamic configuration delivery.\n\n**xDS Types:**\n- **Cluster Discovery Service (CDS)** - Tells proxies about backend services\n- **Endpoint Discovery Service (EDS)** - Lists healthy endpoints for a service\n- **Listener Discovery Service (LDS)** - Defines how to listen for incoming traffic\n- **Route Discovery Service (RDS)** - Defines routing rules\n- **Secret Discovery Service (SDS)** - Delivers TLS certificates\n\n### Data Flow: Service Discovery to xDS Push\n\nHere's an end-to-end example of how a service discovery update triggers an xDS push:\n\n1. **Service Registry Update**\n   - A Kubernetes pod is created in the cluster\n   - Pilot's Kubernetes controller watches the API server\n   - The controller detects the new pod and updates the `ServiceInstance` model\n\n2. **Model Update**\n   - Pilot's `Environment` (in `pilot/pkg/model/context.go`) maintains all discovered services\n   - When a `ServiceInstance` changes, the controller notifies the environment via `XDSUpdater`\n\n3. **Configuration Generation**\n   - The networking layer (`pilot/pkg/networking/`) generates Envoy configuration\n   - For the new endpoint, it creates or updates:\n     - An Envoy `Cluster` (the backend service definition)\n     - `Endpoints` (the specific pod IP and port)\n\n4. **xDS Push**\n   - Pilot's xDS server (in `pilot/pkg/xds/`) maintains connections to all Envoy proxies\n   - When configuration changes, it sends:\n     - **EDS update** with the new endpoint\n     - **CDS update** if the cluster definition changed\n     - **RDS update** if routing rules changed\n   - Each update is accompanied by a version number for consistency checking\n\n5. **Envoy Updates**\n   - Envoy proxies receive the xDS update\n   - They validate and apply the new configuration\n   - Traffic to the new endpoint begins flowing\n\n**Key files for this flow:**\n- `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller.go` - Kubernetes controller watching services/endpoints\n- `pilot/pkg/model/context.go` - The `Environment` and `PushContext` that maintain state\n- `pilot/pkg/networking/core/v1alpha3/` - Config builders for Envoy resources\n- `pilot/pkg/xds/v3/ads.go` - Aggregated Discovery Service (ADS) implementation\n\n### Service Registry Integration\n\nPilot uses an abstraction layer to support multiple service discovery backends:\n\n**Service Registry Interface** (`pilot/pkg/model/service.go`):\n- `ServiceInstance` - A single service instance (pod, VM, etc.)\n- `Service` - A logical service with multiple instances\n- `ServiceRegistry` - Interface for discovering services\n\n**Supported Backends** (`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/`):\n- `kube/` - Kubernetes native service discovery\n- `serviceentry/` - ServiceEntry custom resource\n- `memory/` - In-memory registry (testing)\n- `aggregate/` - Aggregates multiple registries\n\nWhen Pilot starts, it initializes service registries and watches them for changes. The aggregate registry combines multiple sources, allowing a single control plane to work across hybrid environments.\n\n### Key Packages\n\n| Package | Purpose |\n|---------|---------|\n| `pilot/pkg/model/` | Core data models and context |\n| `pilot/pkg/networking/` | Config generation for Envoy |\n| `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/` | Service discovery abstraction |\n| `pilot/pkg/xds/` | xDS protocol implementation |\n| `pilot/pkg/bootstrap/` | Pilot startup and initialization |\n| `security/pkg/pki/` | Certificate generation and management |\n| `pkg/config/` | Istio configuration types and validation |\n| `pkg/kube/` | Kubernetes client utilities |\n\n---\n\n## First Contribution Workflow\n\n### Finding Good First Issues\n\nThe Istio project uses GitHub issues to track work. To find issues suitable for new contributors:\n\n1. Visit [github.com/istio/istio/issues](https://github.com/istio/istio/issues)\n2. Filter by labels:\n   - `good-first-issue` - Ideal for beginners\n   - `help-wanted` - Community help is welcome\n   - `kind/bug` - Bug fixes are always valuable\n3. Check the issue for:\n   - A clear problem statement\n   - Reproduction steps (for bugs)\n   - Expected vs. actual behavior\n\n### Development Workflow\n\n#### 1. Fork and Branch\n\nFork the repository on GitHub and create a feature branch:\n\n```bash\ngit checkout -b fix/issue-name\n```\n\n#### 2. Make Your Changes\n\nEdit the code in your branch. For example, if fixing an issue in Pilot:\n\n```bash\n# Edit the relevant file\nvim pilot/pkg/model/service.go\n\n# Or if it's a test file\nvim pilot/pkg/model/service_test.go\n```\n\n#### 3. Run Pre-commit Checks\n\nBefore committing, run the linters and formatters:\n\n```bash\nmake precommit\n```\n\nThis ensures your code matches Istio's style guide. Run Tests\n\nAlways run tests for the package you modified:\n\n```bash\n# Run tests for a specific package\nPKG=./pilot/pkg/model make test\n\n# Or run tests for a broader area\ngo test -race ./pilot/...\n```\n\nIf you're adding a new feature, add unit tests:\n\n```go\n// In pilot/pkg/model/service_test.go\nfunc TestMyNewFeature(t *testing.T) {\n    // Setup\n    svc := &Service{...}\n\n    // Action\n    result := svc.MyNewMethod()\n\n    // Assert\n    if result != expected {\n        t.Errorf(\"got %v, want %v\", result, expected)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### 5. Use the PR template to auto-assign if available.\n\n#### CI Gates\n\nYour PR will automatically run:\n- **Unit tests** - All tests must pass\n- **Linters** - Code must pass style checks\n- **Build verification** - Binaries must compile on all supported platforms\n\nAll checks must pass before merging.
